## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (ODE rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is an ordinary differential equation for concentration A over time t, which is the standard setup for chemical reaction kinetics. With only (t, A) available, likely models are empirical/elementary rate laws (order in A), reversible/approach-to-equilibrium forms, or time-varying effective rate constants (e.g., catalyst deactivation or changing conditions).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption when reactant is in excess or surface-limited)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay / pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- Second-order decay (self-reaction): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular A + A consumption)
- General n-th order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall reaction order)
- Linear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady state/equilibrium concentration)
- Reversible first-order pair (A ↔ products with equilibrium A_eq): dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 (net forward minus backward with constant back-flux)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (growth with self-limitation, e.g., autocatalysis with depletion)
- Inhibited/limited rate (rational in A): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate limited by saturation or inhibition-like effect without extra species)
- Activation-like threshold in concentration (smooth): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) / (c2 + Abs(A - c1)) (weak change below/near a critical concentration)
- Time-dependent first-order (changing conditions): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (effective rate increases/decreases approximately linearly with time)
- Exponentially time-varying rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (accelerating/decelerating kinetics due to evolving environment/catalyst)
- Stretched-exponential time modulation: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t**c2) * A (nonlinear time evolution of the effective rate)
- Catalyst deactivation / fading activity (rate decays in time): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant decreases over time)
- Mixed-order with baseline source/sink: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A - c2 * A**2 (combines inflow/production with multiple consumption channels)
- Oscillatory forcing of kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (periodic driving, e.g., light modulation in photochemistry)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elementary reaction order identification: dA_dt proportional to A, A**2, or A**n indicates uni-/bi-molecular or lumped overall order behavior.
- Approach-to-equilibrium/steady state: dependence on (A - c) suggests relaxation toward a fixed point concentration (stable if coefficient is negative).
- Presence of a constant term (±c0) in dA_dt implies external feed/production or constant-loss processes (e.g., zero-order regimes).
- Time-varying rate constants: factors like (c0 + c1*t) or exp(±c*t) multiplying A indicate changing conditions (catalyst activation/deactivation, ramped control).
- Self-limiting/autocatalytic behavior: A*(c - A) structure implies an interior stable/unstable fixed point and nonlinear feedback in concentration evolution.
- Rate limitation at high concentration: rational forms A/(A+c) imply diminishing returns (effective rate plateaus) as A grows large.
- Multiple pathways: sums of different powers (e.g., -c1*A - c2*A**2) suggest parallel mechanisms with different molecularities.
- Periodic forcing signatures: sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) modulation implies externally driven kinetics (e.g., light, mixing cycles) rather than intrinsic mass-action only.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK28)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A*exp(-c1*_s*t) + c2*_z*A**c3/(c4*A**c5 + c6)
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(t,A)=\frac{0.7391218893\,A^2}{0.8913296034\,A^4+1}\;-\;0.300937047\,A\,e^{-0.0677673962\,t}.
\]
Key structural facts:
- It is a **sum of two terms**: (i) a **rational function of \(A\) only** with shape \(k\,A^2/(mA^4+1)\), and (ii) an **\(A\cdot e^{-\lambda t}\)** term.
- There is **no** \(\log(\cdot)\), **no** \(\sin(\cdot)\), **no** \(t\) polynomial factors, **no** \(t/(A+\cdot)^5\), **no** \(1/\sqrt{A}\), and **no** \(e^{A\cdot}\).
- Any candidate containing such extra functional forms must set their coefficients to 0; then the remaining forms must still be able to produce both the rational-in-\(A\) term and the \(A e^{-\lambda t}\) term.

Now check each candidate.

1. Contains \(A^{c0}c1\), \(e^{c3 t}\log(\cdot)\), \(e^{A c6}\), \(t/(A+c8)^5\), \(1/\sqrt A\). Can zero out extras, but remaining is just a monomial \(A^{c0}\) (times constant). Cannot produce \(A^2/(mA^4+1)\) nor \(A e^{-\lambda t}\). **No**.

2. After zeroing log/exp(A) terms, left with monomials and an \(A^{c2}t\) term. Cannot create rational \(A^2/(mA^4+1)\) or \(A e^{-\lambda t}\). **No**.

3. Similar: only monomials + \(t\) times monomial + exp(A) + log term. No way to get rational-in-\(A\) or \(A e^{-\lambda t}\). **No**.

4. Only sums of monomials and \(t\) monomial plus log term. No rational, no \(A e^{-\lambda t}\). **No**.

5. Linear in \(A\), monomials, \(t\) monomial, exp(A), log term. Even if log/exp(A)/t terms removed, left with polynomial/monomial in \(A\), not \(A^2/(mA^4+1)\). Also no \(e^{-\lambda t}\) term. **No**.

22. Has \(A c0 (c1+t)^{c2}\) (power of affine \(t\)), monomials, log-exponential. No way to get \(e^{-\lambda t}\) (power is not exponential), and no rational-in-\(A\). **No**.

23. This is the only one with a rational-looking structure. Simplify:
\[
\frac{A^6 c0 + A^6 c3 E + A^5 c6 E + A^5 c7 + A c8 t + c9 t}{A^6 c1 + A^5 c2},
\]
where \(E=\exp(c4 t)\log(c5 t+1)\).
Factor \(A^5\) in denominator: \(A^5(Ac1+c2)\). Then expression becomes
\[
\frac{A(c0+c3E) + (c6E+c7) + \frac{c8 t}{A^4} + \frac{c9 t}{A^5}}{A c1 + c2}.
\]
GT’s rational term is \(\frac{kA^2}{mA^4+1}\), which has denominator \(mA^4+1\) (quartic in \(A\) plus constant), not linear \(A c1+c2\), and no negative powers \(A^{-4},A^{-5}\). You could set \(c8=c9=0\) and kill \(E\) by setting \(c3=c6=0\), leaving \(\frac{A c0 + c7}{A c1 + c2}\), still a linear-over-linear rational function, not \(A^2/(mA^4+1)\). Also no \(A e^{-\lambda t}\) term. **No**.

Could set log term and \(t/(A+\cdot)^5\) to 0, leaving \(A^{c0}c1 + c5 e^{c6 t} + c9\). But GT needs \(A e^{-\lambda t}\) (product of \(A\) and exponential), not a sum of separate \(A\)-only and \(t\)-only terms. **No**.

29. Has linear \(A\) terms, log-exponential, constant, exp(A), \(t/(A+\cdot)^5\). No. **No**.

None of the candidates can generate the required **quartic-denominator rational in \(A\)** term \(kA^2/(mA^4+1)\) *and* the required **product** term \(-\alpha A e^{-\lambda t}\) without introducing forbidden structures (logs, exp(A), sine, inverse powers, or \(t/(A+\cdot)^5\)), and no candidate has the needed functional building blocks to do so.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK28)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A*exp(-c1*_s*t) + c2*_z*A**c3/(c4*A**c5 + c6)
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze whether any candidate can exactly match the Ground Truth:

$$GT = \frac{0.7391 A^2}{0.8913 A^4 + 1} - 0.3009 A \cdot e^{-0.06776 t}$$

The GT has two terms:
1. A rational function of A: $\frac{c \cdot A^2}{d \cdot A^4 + 1}$
2. An exponential decay in t multiplied by A: $-c_0 \cdot A \cdot e^{-c_1 t}$

Key structural features:
- Term 1 is a rational function in A (not polynomial, not exponential, not log, not trig)
- Term 2 is $A \cdot e^{-\alpha t}$ — a product of A and a pure exponential in t

Let me check each candidate's basis functions against these requirements.

**Critical observation about Term 2:** $-0.3009 A \cdot e^{-0.06776 t}$ — this is $A$ times a decaying exponential in $t$. None of the candidates seem to have a term of the form $A \cdot \exp(c \cdot t)$. Let me look more carefully.

Most candidates have terms like:
- $\exp(c \cdot t) \cdot \log(c \cdot t + 1)$ — this is NOT equivalent to $\exp(c \cdot t)$ alone
- $A^{c_0} \cdot c_1 \cdot t$ — polynomial in t, not exponential
- $\exp(A \cdot c)$ — exponential in A, not t
- $t/(A+c)^5$ — rational in A, polynomial in t

**Can $\exp(c_1 t) \cdot \log(c_2 t + 1)$ equal $A \cdot \exp(\alpha t)$?** No — this has no A dependence, and $\log(c_2 t + 1)$ cannot be absorbed into the exponential to produce a pure exponential.

**Can any combination of the candidate terms produce $A \cdot e^{-\alpha t}$?** This requires a term that is simultaneously linear in A and exponential in t. Looking through all candidates:

- Candidates with $A \cdot c \cdot t$ terms have polynomial (not exponential) t-dependence
- Candidates with $\exp(c \cdot t) \cdot \log(c \cdot t + 1)$ have no A dependence
- Candidate 22 has $A \cdot c_0 \cdot (c_1 + t)^{c_2}$ — power law in t, not exponential
- Candidate 23 has complex rational structure but all terms are rational in A and involve $t$ or $\exp \cdot \log$ — no pure $A \cdot e^{ct}$
- Candidate 28 has $\exp(c_6 t)$ but with no A dependence

**For Term 1:** $\frac{A^2}{c \cdot A^4 + 1}$ — this is a specific rational function. Terms like $t/(A+c)^5$, $1/\sqrt{A}$, $\log(A \cdot c + 1)$, $\sin(A)$, $\exp(A \cdot c)$, or power laws $A^{c_0}$ cannot reproduce this rational function structure.

**No candidate has both:**
1. A rational function $A^2/(A^4 + c)$ structure
2. A term $A \cdot \exp(c \cdot t)$

Since the GT requires these two specific basis functions and no candidate contains both (or even one of them in the correct form), none can match.

Let me verify candidates with $\exp(A \cdot c)$: Could $\exp(A \cdot c)$ with $c \to 0$ approximate the rational function? No — setting $c=0$ gives a constant, not a rational function of A. We need EXACT equivalence.

After careful analysis of all 50 candidates, none can produce both required terms of the GT.
